Asset forfeiture, as established under various state and federal statutes, is intended 
to disrupt criminal activities through the seizure and forfeiture of the instruments or pr
oceeds of crime. 
Pursuant to California Health and Safety Code section 11495, the California Department of Justice (DOJ) publishes an annual report providing information on forfeiture actions during the preceding calendar year. This 27th annual report covers the 2021 calendar year.  The DOJ sends an annual request to all local law enforcement agencies and district attorneys’ offices for the federal and state seizure and forfeiture information.  The DOJ received federal seizure and forfeiture information from 121 out of approximately 400 state and local law enforcement agencies, and state seizure and forfeiture information from 42 out of 58 district attorneys’ offices.  Local law enforcement agencies and district attorneys’ offices are not statutorily mandated to provide their data to the DOJ for inclusion in the annual report. 
Health and Safety Code section 1 1 495 
11495(a) The funds received by the law enforcement agencies under section 11489 shall be deposited into an account maintained by the Controller, county auditor, or city treasurer. These funds shall be distributed to the law enforcement agencies at their request. The Controller, auditor, or treasurer shall maintain a record of these disbursements which records shall be open to public inspection, subject to the privileges contained in sections 1040, 1041, and 1042 of the Evidence Code. 
(b) Upon request of the governing body of the jurisdiction in which the distributions are 
made, the Controller, auditor, or treasurer shall conduct an audit of these funds and their use. In the case of the state, the governing body shall be the Legislature. 
(c) Each year, the Attorney General shall publish a report which sets forth the following 
information for the state, each county, each city, and each city and county: 
(1) The number of forfeiture actions initiated and administered by state or local 
agencies under California law, the number of cases adopted by the federal 
government, and the number of cases initiated by a joint federal-state action that were prosecuted under federal law. 
(2) The number of cases and the administrative number or court docket number of 
each case for which forfeiture was ordered or declared. 
1  
 
 
 
 
 
continued 
(3) T he number of suspects charged with a controlled substance violation. 
(4) The number of alleged criminal offenses that were under federal or state law. (5) The disposition of cases, including no charge, dropped charges, acquittal, plea 
agreement, jury conviction, or other. 
(6) The value of the assets forfeited. (7) The recipients of the forfeited assets, the amounts received, and the date of the 
disbursement. 
(d)The Attorney General shall develop administrative guidelines for the collection and 
publication of the information required in subdivision (c). 
(e) The Attorney General’s report shall cover the calendar year and shall be made no 
later than July 1 of each year beginning with the year after the enactment of this law. 
2  
  
  
 
 
 
 
Statistics were solicited from California’s district attorneys’ offices and law enforcement 
agencies. Although the DOJ is required to prepare this report, local agencies are not s
tatutorily mandated to provide their data to the DOJ for inclusion. The 2021 report 
reflects the responses that were received from 42 district attorneys and 121 state and local law enforcement agencies. In California, there are 58 district attorneys and approximately 400 law enforcement agencies. Based on the data received by the DOJ, the following highlights the findings in this report: 
• A total of 2,770 state forfeiture proceedings were initiated in 2021 (Table 1). 
• A total of 2,449 federal forfeiture sharing requests were submitted in 2021 (Table 4). 
• A total of 2,144 state forfeiture cases were completed during 2021, which included 
cases initiated in 2021 and prior years. The total value of the disbursed assets is $33,782,687.89 (Table 2). 
• A total of 677 joint federal asset forfeiture cases in which state or local law 
enforcement participated were completed and disbursed during 2021. The total value of the federal equitable sharing funds received is $11,799,102.79 (Table 5). 
• Mono County reported no state forfeiture cases initiated or completed in 2021 
(Table 3). 
• The following sixteen counties did not participate in providing data for this report: 
Alpine, Calaveras, Del Norte, Fresno, Mariposa, Merced, Modoc, Nevada, Plumas, San Benito,  Sierra, Siskiyou, Solano, Tuolumne, Yolo and Yuba. 
• A total of 121 state and local law enforcement agencies participated in this report, 
64 of which reported no federal equitable sharing funds received (Table 4). 
3  
 
 
 
    
    
    
  
        
    
     
   
    
  
  
 
To comply with the requirements of Health and Safety Code section 11495, the DOJ 
reached out to all California district attorneys, who are the officials conducting state f
orfeiture proceedings, to request that they provide the DOJ with the required information 
for each state forfeiture action conducted during the reporting period. Although the DOJ is required to prepare this report, local agencies are not statutorily mandated to provide their data to the DOJ for inclusion. 
This report provides the information required by Health and Safety Code section 11495 
on all forfeitures initiated during calendar year 2021. For state forfeitures completed and federal distributions received during calendar year 2021, detailed information is provided. 
Pursuant to Health and Safety Code section 11489, state asset forfeiture proceeds are 
distributed as follows: 
• One percent to a private, nonprofit organization composed of local prosecutors for the exclusive purpose of providing a statewide program of education and training 
for prosecutors and law enforcement in the ethics and proper use of state asset forfeiture laws. 
• Ten percent to the prosecutorial agency that processes the forfeiture action.  
• Twenty-four percent to the state General Fund. 
• Sixty-five percent to the state and/or local law enforcement agencies that participated in the seizure of the assets, distributed in a manner that reflects the proportionate contribution of each agency. Fifteen percent
1 of the funds distributed to law 
enforcement must be deposited in a special fund which is maintained by a council made up of local government entities. This fund shall be used for the sole purpose of funding programs designed to combat drug abuse and divert gang activity. 
1 Although local agencies are not statutorily mandated to provide their data to the DOJ for inclusion, some did provide information regarding their 1 5 percent deposit into a special fund (Table 3).

Information regarding Federal Equitable Sharing sought and received by California law 
enforcement agencies through joint investigations can only be obtained directly from the participating agencies. This is the fourth report to include federal forfeiture data and the fourth time agencies other than district attorneys’ offices have been called upon to participate. 
Federal asset forfeiture proceeds received by a state or local law enforcement agency may 
be utilized for allowable law enforcement purposes as defined in the Federal Guide to Equitable Sharing. Health and Safety Code section 11471.2 prohibits state and local law enforcement agencies from seeking federal adoption of specified asset seizures. It also prohibits acceptance of certain federal equitable sharing distributions when the asset seized is real property or less than $40,000 in cash or other negotiable instruments, unless the underlying criminal case has resulted in a conviction. When such prohibited seizures are ordered forfeited, the participating California agency must decline or return the distribution. In those cases, the entire forfeited amount is retained by the federal agency.

• For purposes of this report, seizure of assets or completing a federal sharing request 
constitutes the initiation of a forfeiture action. 
• Initiated cases may result in forfeitures in the 2021 reporting year or remain pending 
after 2021. 
• Table 1 provides information on asset forfeiture actions initiated pursuant to California law during 2021 and is also reflective of information reported by district attorney’s offices (Page 10). 
• Table 4 provides information on forfeiture sharing requests initiated as a part of a joint federal asset forfeiture investigation during 2021 (Page 309).

• For purposes of this report, an asset forfeiture case is considered completed when 
forfeiture has been ordered or declared and all assets have been distributed2 by the 
district attorney’s office or federal sharing funds have been received3 . 
• Table 2 provides summary information on asset forfeiture actions completed 
pursuant to California law during 2021. This includes disbursement information on cases initiated in 2021 and prior years (Page 14). 
• Table 3 is the most extensive section within this report and provides detailed information on each asset forfeiture case that was completed pursuant to state law during 2021 (Page 16). 
• Table 5 provides summary information on federal asset forfeitures received by state and local law enforcement agencies as part of a joint asset forfeiture case in 2021, including cases initiated in 2021 and prior years (Page 314). 
• Table 6 provides detailed information on federal asset forfeiture cases for which equitable sharing funds were disbursed to California law enforcement agencies during 2021 (Page 316). 
• Cases for which only a partial distribution was made during 2021 are not listed in Tables 3 or 6, as they are considered still pending. They will be reported once they are fully distributed. 
• Tables 2 and 3 reflect data reported by district attorney’s offices. 
• Tables 4, 5, and 6 reflect data reported by law enforcement agencies. 
2 When all seized items have been returned to the defendant following adjudication of a previously initiated case, it is no longer considered to be an asset forfeiture case. 
3 Federal sharing funds that a state or local law enforcement agency has returned to the federal sharing agency are not considered funds received and are not included in this report.
